{"kind": "blogger#postList", "nextPageToken": "CgkIChjA99uq1SUQy4Ca9ZL8nrwx", "items": [{"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "6656068422884288381", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-01-12T12:51:00+05:30", "updated": "2011-01-12T12:51:49+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMjk0ODE2OTA5MTU5Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/01/meg-fibre-grade-on-chemical-tankers.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/6656068422884288381", "title": "MEG FIBRE GRADE ON CHEMICAL TANKERS -- CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div class=\"MsoNormal\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TS1VsBcNczI/AAAAAAAACtA/hus4RCjK1x0/s1600/chm.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TS1VsBcNczI/AAAAAAAACtA/hus4RCjK1x0/s1600/chm.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nThis post is written in great detail , to show the uninitiated that MEG FG is a special cargo. There are many who have learnt it the hard way.<br />\n<br />\nMEG industrial grade is NOT a difficult cargo-- BUT Union carbide coprn MEG fibre grade is!<br />\n<br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">MEG FG is by far the cleanest cargo a chemical man will carry.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The Wall wash specs for UCC are very stringent.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Chris/ EGC<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Pollution category/ Y<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">USCG group/ 20<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">BP/ 197<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">MP/ -12 C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">FP/ 240 C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">AH/ 40 C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">SG/ 1.13<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Basic items required to properly clean to MEG FG specifications:--<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Sufficient low ppm (less than 10 ppm) chloride fresh water<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">A properly functioning fresh water generator (evaporator), and a proper functioning compressor and air supply system able to supply clean air.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Proper equipment with which to clean and test the tanks.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">A proper functioning steam system producing steam with nil hydrocarbon, nil chlorides. With sufficient capacity to heat the coils to dry tanks,&nbsp; and a proper functioning butterworth heater.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Sufficient cleaning chemicals to clean the tanks.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">An enthusiastic and trained crew<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Let us first look at the cleanliness requirements, wall wash specifications, foot sample specifications and final specifications. We will also look at the methods of conducting the wall wash and shipboard equivalents to the shore lab so that we may duplicate the tests as close as possible.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">A typical wallwash procedure or MEG FG is given in my blog site.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Wall wash specifications for union carbide MEG FG:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; color: red; font-size: large;\">Chlorides&nbsp; :&nbsp; less than 0.249 ppm ( ridiculous but true! )</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Color: less than 10 platinum cobalt<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Suspended matter: less than 6-8 particulate that are no greater than the diameter of a common pencil lead in size.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Hydrocarbons: nil, clear and no foam remaining on top when vigorously shaken.&nbsp; 50% di-water/ 50% wall wash solution.&nbsp; Look down through the liquid from the top of cylinder to the bottom and compare to a cylinder with pure test methanol only. Do this in against a black and white background. (you can put a white paper with writing on it underneath)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Note: if you have the presence of slight hydrocarbons you may find out that you have left over cleaning chemicals on the bulkheads by making 90% di water and 10% wallwash. Then shake vigorously. The presence of foam remaining on top for over 30 seconds indicates some cleaning solution or detergent left in the coating.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">It is important to have sufficient di water in order to spray all tanks at least twice for 3 hrs. Each. Low chloride water can be made on board in the following manner:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Start with 10-15 ppm water and recirculate on a continuous basis through a di-water generator. This can be done by placing a di-water generator near an outside faucet or use a wilden M-2 pump and suck up from the fresh water tank and run the water through the filter and return to the fresh water fill line.&nbsp; It is important that this system is isolated from the rest of the ships supply so that it is not inadvertently contaminated.&nbsp; Also you can speed the process along by entering newly produced water from the evaporator and consuming from this tank. This must be monitored very closely. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Make sure everyone is aware of the process so that everyone understands the importance of what is going on. You must test the water every few hours (both inlet and outlet) so that you can be sure that the di -water generator is not saturated with chlorides and not working.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">You should be able to reduce chlorides in approximately 150 mt fresh water from 10-15 ppm to less than 4 ppm over a 5-10 day period. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Of course the best way to have good water is to use ships FWG water.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Air supply system- this must be able to deliver sufficient air to run four Dasic jet fan 65 tank vent fans. Also it must be able to supply clean air for airline breathing apparatus and to run the 10:1 ratio barrel pump to full pressure (7kg/cm2)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Any leaking hoses or equipment that must be worked on continuously is unacceptable. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">All air and&nbsp; steam driven equipment used in and around the cargo tank should have an exhaust hose attached to direct waste air or steam away from the tank so that it is not drawn back into the tank. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Compressed air from the ships supply contains vaporized oil and other contaminants that may contaminate your tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If the weather is&nbsp; rainy and cold&nbsp; it is almost impossible to dry tanks without the heating coils properly functioning.the steam system must be able to produce steam that is chloride and hydrocarbon free.&nbsp; This is accomplished by stopping the use of boiler treatment chemicals two-three days prior to use. You must carefully test the condensate before use for hydrocarbons and chlorides. Once free of chlorides and hydrocarbons, the steam can be used to steam tanks and cargo lines.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">A careful check of steam condensate will also alert you to possible leaks in heating coils and contamination of same. During steaming, the steam should be tested at least once per day and always upon restarting steaming after shutting down.&nbsp; All steaming of tanks, cargo lines, p/v vent lines should be completed prior to using the heating coils to dry tanks. The reason for this is there may be contamination of heating coils by previous cargo and if coils are opened prior to completion of steaming tanks, you may end up contaminating all cargo tanks being steamed.while steaming your tanks the cargo pumps should be run intermittently in order to avoid buildup of condensate in the tank. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When determining the cleaning chemicals required, there are several factors which come into play.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Last three to five cargoes carried in each tank to br prepared<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Coating condition of cargo tanks<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Cargo line condition<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Present tank cleanliness<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Cargo vent line condition<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Remember, there is no substitute for hot butterworth. The most important thing to remember is to order cleaning chemicals at least two weeks prior to requiring them. This is to allow your ship operator to make necessary arrangements.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The participation of the Master and all crew members working together as a team is the key to success. You must keep an exact record of your daily cleaning progress and what was or was not accomplished each day. Include time used for rigging, equipment breakdowns etc.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Typical wall wash lab items:-</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">1) Reagent Silver Nitrate\u2014strength 10% /&nbsp; 250 cc \u20132 Bottles<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">2) Reagent Nitric acid --- strength 20% / 500 cc- 2 bottles<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">3) Reagent Potassium Permanganate crystals \u2013 0.1 gms in stoppered tubes/ 12 tubes<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;for making 0.02% solution on the spot. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">4) Reagent Standard chloride solution ---strength 10 ppm/ 500cc\u20142 bottles<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">5) 5 Apha, 10 Apha, 15 Apha--Standard comparator solution in stoppered tubes <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">6) pH value paper colour comparator strips 1 to 14\u20144 boxes<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">7) Nessler tube with round bottom 100 CC &nbsp;and white markings / 16 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">8) Stand for above tubes<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">9) Nessler tube with flat bottom stand 50 CC/ &nbsp;24 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">10) Polyethylene methanol wall wash squirt bottles 500 cc/ 4 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">11) Polyethylene wall wash funnel with flat side and 60 deg angle short stem/ 4 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">12) Pipette glass pyrex brand 5 CC/ 4 nos ( graduated)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">13) Pipette glass pryes brand 10 cc/ 4 nos&nbsp; ( graduated )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">14) Conc Hydrochloric acid/ 500 CC<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">15) Lab grade methanol&nbsp; chlorides &lt; 0.05 ppm / 60 litres<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">16) &nbsp;DI water/ 60 litres<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">17) Thermometer 0 to 100 deg C/ 3 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">18) Ice box portable with white interior to hold at least 12 nessler 100 CC tubes vertically<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">19) Sample bottles wide mouth transparent glass 500 CC/12 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">20) Wall wash plastic bucket/ 2 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">21) Parasol wide 2 metres dia/2 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">22) Washing brush for nessler tube/ 2 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">23) Penlite torch / 2 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">24) Disposable vinyl gloves/ 100 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">25) Disposable shoe covers plastic\u2014lint free / 100 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">26) Filter paper 5A and Whatman 42# 10 cm paper filter qualitative, white / 100 nos each<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">27) Palladium chloride solution/ 50 cc<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">28) Disposable 5CC pipettes\u2014100 nos<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">29) Lab grade acetone ( for NVM and Plankton of sea water )\u2014 20 litres<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">30) Stainless steel funnel / 2 nos <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">31) Sponges for Lint free mopping and wiping steam coil bottoms.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">32) Methanol Draeger tubes&nbsp; 50ppm \u20133000 ppm range / 50 nos ( expiry dates to note )<o:p></o:p></span></div><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Reporting your results.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">While preparing your tanks you will send a daily progress report to your ship operator. You will advise him on your tank cleaning progress to date and any wall wash tests results. It is important that you advise the cleaning methods used, number of hours butterworthed( hot or cold), any problems you are having. This will enable us to help you with cleaning advice and assist with solutions to your problems. We are also in contact with the supercargo who will also advise on cleaning. Wall wash test results should be reported as follows:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Tank&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; HC&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Cl&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; PTT&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Color<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Nbr<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">1P&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; slight&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 1 ppm&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 47 min&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 10<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">***you will also keep a daily cleaning log with test results .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">***reporting on color: this may be difficult to determine to the untrained eye.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">&nbsp;You should compare to a methanol standard with a white background and white florescent light.&nbsp; It may be beneficial to report if you can see evidence of color in the wall wash collection jar. Also you can report for example: same as standard : clear,&nbsp; almost as clear as sample: slight.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When you are at the loading port, if the ship operator or supercargo is not present, the master or chief officer should go with the surveyor to the lab to witness the testing.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">This is important especially in the event tanks fail for foam or hydrocarbons.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The reason for this is so that you can see&nbsp; how bad the foam is and also same for hydrocarbons. If you don\u2019t go, then all you will have to work with just the report from surveyors that tanks have failed.There are degrees of how bad the foam is (heavy foam, light, very light)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Sometimes the tank will fail on hydrocarbons, chlorides, foam) if the test was taken with damp bulkheads.&nbsp; We have had this happen and all that was done was to let the tank dry out more (with heating coils on and vent fans running) and retest and the tank passed.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Cargo tank dryness is one of the most important keys to getting your wallwash passed if your tanks are clean.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If your bulkheads are wet, you will most likely show presence of chlorides and sometime hydrocarbons. If you are close on your chlorides (less than 1 ppm) and your bulkheads are damp, sometimes all that is needed is longer drying time.&nbsp; You can accomplish this by turning on heating coils and running your tank vent fans. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">In rain and cold, drying tanks is difficult and care must be taken to cover tank tops with tarps and the same goes for your fans. The other problem with the weather and cold in the winter is the possibility of condensation freezing in the cargo pipelines. It is important to keep all drains open and let drain during the day.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">After spraying tanks with di-water and ready for wall wash test</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">All cargo line and vent line drains and manifolds open to drain out condensation.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Turn on heating coils to aid in drying tanks<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Have airline ready to blow down drop line into cargo tanks. This is so surveyors can check to see if the line is clear. Make sure spray equipment is ready in case of tank failure.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Seal with silicon all butterworth plates except forward most plate. Leave tank top unsealed. ( Silicon work is NOT necessary on butterworth ports with double seal and check nuts )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Once tank has passed wallwash seal up the forward butterworth plate. Remove all water from tanks, mop and dry. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Also remove any dust and contaminants. Check all drain lines to remove every drop of water. Look from tank top into vent line.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Blank steam coils only after the WWT has passed. Surveyor will not enter unless the TLV of methanol ( if methanol sparyed ) is &gt;70% of methanol used. Same way cargo hoses must not be connected till the wall wash has passed. Once hoses are connected no entry is allowed into tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Once all tanks have passed wall wash make a final check again of all tanks, lines for water. Close all drains and tank tops. Do not seal tank tops yet, this will come after final nitrogen purging. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Have airline breathing apparatus ready for use on deck. Once cargo hose is connected and airblow is done, and nitrogen purge started look down into each tank and see if any free water has come out of cargo drop line into tank. If so, tell shore to stop nitrogen purge, disconnect cargo loading hose and put on air breathing apparatus and mop up water in tank. Then, when all out of tank you can reconnect loading hose and resume purging. If spare tank is available, the take first shot of nitrogen into that tank<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Sometimes a small amount of meg is blown into the cargo tanks from the shore hose. Only cargo lines are blown with nitrogen before loading. All nitrogen purging and blanketing is done after loading completes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Initially the cargo is taken into the pipelines and contents deslopped. It is vessels responsibility to provide deslopping drums. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">It is ships call when to stop loading for taking the first foot sample.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Upon completion of loading the cargo tanks will be purged down to 7% oxygen content. The best way to do this is to start this in a slack tank so that the loading line can be cleared of product without risk of overflow.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When purging with nitrogen keep pv valve lifted and the tank dome open by 2 inches to prevent structural damage to tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Pressurize each MEG FG tank in turn after all&nbsp; tanks have been taken down to 7% oxygen.&nbsp; When last tank is being taken down to 7% oxygen have a person stand by the first tank to be pressurized and have dock close down nitrogen pressure to about one quarter open.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Reduce nitrogen flow to 20% open.&nbsp; Tank valve and start pressurizing have a person near p/v valve to make sure it is lifting . When relief valve lifts , open next tank and close down tank valve.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When last tank\u2019s p/v valve lifts, have shore shut down nitrogen and close tank valve.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Have shore bleed off pressure and disconnect shore hose.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Test all deck openings for leaks with ultrasonic probe.&nbsp; You will keep a daily nitrogen pressure log of the nitrogen pressure in each tank during the loaded voyage. If a tank falls to zero pressure introduce enough nitrogen to raise pressure to a positive pressure.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Also you will make daily rounds on deck to check for leaks with the ultraprobe.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Regarding ultraprobe:&nbsp; this unit is a very sensitive listening device that picks up leaks around seals and joints. This unit is fragile so care must be taken to keep it from banging around. This ultraprobe costs around $4500.00 USD to replace.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Before discharge checklist:--<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Approximately 1-2hrs prior to picking up pilot at first discharge port open all MEG FG manifolds and drains.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Start each pump and run a small amount of cargo out through each manifold. Examine for particles and floaters. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If everything is clear, then shut down and drain lines.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">When surveyor comes on board, you will note his method of sampling. Any deviation from sampling methods employed by the surveyors from the way it is usually&nbsp; done will be noted with a protest. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Also fax to ship operator the statement of sampling methods as shown below signed by chief officer and surveyor.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Statement of sampling methods<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Ship name:_________________________&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; voy:________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Port: ______________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Date: ______________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Cargo:____________________________ <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Material of sample bottle: (glass, plastic)_________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">2. Material of sampling apparatus&nbsp; pot&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; _________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Material of sampling line (s.s., cotton, fiber)______________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Were bottles flushed with product (yes,no)_______________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">5. Were sample bottles new (yes, no)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Were bottles checked for foreign particles______________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Material of gloves used (plastic,rubber, none)____________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">8. Depth of cargo where sample was drawn&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">9. Samples taken in the presence of&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">10. Other observations: <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">(oxygen content of each tank opened&nbsp;&nbsp; tank- o2<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">(weather conditions at time of sampling)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">_____________________________________&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ______________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Chief officer&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; surveyor<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The supercargo or chief officer is always to follow the surveyor inside the tank and observe the surveyor.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Watch and make sure the surveyor cleans and rinses all equipment such as the bottle, funnel, cap, hands with methanol prior to taking wallwash in each tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Be diplomatic when asking the surveyor to do the above when he forgets.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If the surveyor scrapes or slides the funnel against the coating there is a good possibility that the wall wash test will fail on suspended matter, especially on zinc coating. Request a retest if the tank fails. Also you may ask the surveyor to \u201cjump\u201d the funnel down the side of the tank rather than to scrape it down. (this means to bring the funnel away from the wall and bring it against the wall at a lower place).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Watch for the surveyors touching the funnel with their hands when putting the funnel back into the plastic bag.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">(if they do touch with their hands, make sure they wash with methanol before reuse in the next tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Assume that the surveyors oxygen meter does not work very well during final purging, and double check with the vessels oxygen meter.&nbsp; This is especially important during wet weather when their sensor is thrown off by moisture.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Maintenance of cargo quality during the voyage:---<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The following procedures will be carried out on all vessels carrying MEG FG<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Our main problem at this time is elevated chlorides at discharge port.&nbsp; It should be noted that the chloride spec is considered to be elevated if the discharge tank sample has 0.10 ppm increase in chloride as compared to the final load sample at load port.&nbsp; The main source of increase in chlorides would be a leak of salt water into the tank on the voyage or chlorides remaining on the overhead and ullage space of the tank that are not immersed in product at the load berth but get \u201cwashed down\u201d while the vessel is at sea.&nbsp; Therefore, it is imperative that tanks are di-water washed completely (not just areas accessible to wall washing) during final cleaning.&nbsp; Tanks will be sealed with silicon or shrink wrap if necessary on completion of loading and nitrogen pressure maintained during the voyage.&nbsp; To accomplish this zero tolerance level of cargo quality, we require the following procedures to be followed:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The chief mate or other designated cargo officer must maintain a cleaning and sealing record/log of each MEG FG tank and must sign off on this document that all cleaning and sealing has been witnessed in person.&nbsp; We can not accept the word of the crew member doing the work, it must be witnessed.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">After completion loading, the cargo officer will personally witness the nitrogen purging and oxygen level and check each tank for leaks with the ultra sonic probe.&nbsp; The vessel is to stay at the load berth until the cargo officer is convinced that the tanks are tight and the nitrogen pressure is holding.&nbsp; The results of this inspection will be the first entry on the vessels\u2019 nitrogen log and is to be signed by the cargo officer.&nbsp; Once again if this procedure takes more time than anticipated and the vessel misses the tide, so be it. Let nobody rush you.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">During the voyage, the cargo officer must record daily nitrogen pressures and check for leaks with the ultra sonic probe each day when weather permits.&nbsp; Nitrogen log entries are to be factual and signed daily by the cargo officer and record days when weather did not permit actual on deck checking.&nbsp; If a tank loses pressure, it should be recorded together with action taken to find the leak. It is foolishness to have a \u201cperfect\u201d nitrogen log unless it actually happens.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">At the discharge port, the cargo officer must personally supervise ullaging and sampling and insure that the discharging surveyor draws an extra sample and seals it for the vessel to retain. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Tankcleaning after discharge:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Cold wash for 30 minutes<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Hotwash for one hour<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">FW rinse<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Steam<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Vent<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TS1UmHIXWRI/AAAAAAAACs0/ukDPmRZyiCE/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TS1UmHIXWRI/AAAAAAAACs0/ukDPmRZyiCE/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 years in command )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">..<o:p></o:p></span></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">\n<br />\nBelow a tablet found in Mohenjodaro 4000 BC of Lord Shiva ( Pashupati ).<br />\n<br />\n</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SejEMjkowTM/TsKU5ox4bXI/AAAAAAAAIjw/MJBGhMYf3-s/s1600/imagesCABDGIG9.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"400\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SejEMjkowTM/TsKU5ox4bXI/AAAAAAAAIjw/MJBGhMYf3-s/s400/imagesCABDGIG9.jpg\" width=\"299\" /></a></span></div>\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">\n</span>\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Every year we get to see more and more theories about the Stonehenge -- &nbsp;propounded by the vested interests.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Everybody is tripping over each other to find new meanings for this simple sacrifice spot structure.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Some say it is a bigger wonder than the pyramids-- when in that era, &nbsp;in that entire region, &nbsp;mathematics was unknown.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">This area had come out from the Quaternary ice age only in 9000 BC.</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; Unlike humans, it has the \u201csuperpower\u201d of regenerating its limbs, spinal cord, heart, and other organs..<br /><br />Young frogs are known to regrow limbs, though they lose this ability when they change from tadpoles to adult frogs. On the other hand, the axolotl retains it throughout its entire life, making it unique among vertebrates<br /><br />Humans have also been known to regenerate the tips of the fingers, including the bone and skin. I once lost the tip of my left forefinger on the ship--it has regrown fully.<br /><br />BECAUSE OF CHEMICAL POLLUTION FOR TANNERIES, GANGES MACROPHAGES HAVE LOST THEIR ANCIENT POWERS OF REGENERATION..<br /><br />Injecting a drug to get rid of macrophages in an axolotl\u2019s limb before amputation leads to the accumulation of scar tissue instead of regrowth..<br /><br />This scarring, which happens when a protein called collagen becomes disordered, is a normal part of wound healing in humans, but it is unusual in axolotls. This result suggests that macrophages are essential for regeneration<br /><br />Axolotls stay 'babies' for their whole lives. Axolotls are neotenic creatures meaning they achieve sexual maturity without losing any of their larval features<br /><br />If an axolotl is given a shot of iodine, it will experience a rush of hormones that triggers the animal's growth processes, and it will \"grow up\" and resemble a mature tiger salamander, their closest relative.<br /><br />However, this is not the axolotl's natural state. \"Grown-up\" axolotls are typically listless and die about a year after the injection.<br /><br />Axolotls can regenerate pretty much any body part. A number of amphibians are capable of regenerating limbs, but axolotls take this habit up a notch by regenerating jaws, spinal cords, skin and even portions of their brain. Axolotls can also receive organ transplants and will not reject the new organ.<br /><br />Axolotls have a genome 10 times the size of the human genome..<br /><br /><span style=\"color: red;\">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B0GJOjfYn74</span><br /><br />capt ajit vadakayil<br />..</div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_72MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_72MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\n\n<li class=\"comment\" id=\"bc_0_70B\" kind=\"b\" style=\"background-color: #eeeeee; margin: 0px 0px 16px; padding: 16px 0px 8px;\"><div class=\"comment-block\" id=\"c1061350286957344881\" style=\"margin-left: 48px; position: relative;\">\n<div class=\"comment-header\" id=\"bc_0_70M\" kind=\"m\" style=\"margin: 0px 0px 8px;\">\n<cite class=\"user\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-weight: bold;\"><a href=\"https://www.blogger.com/profile/17821568266464145690\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">CK</a></cite><span class=\"icon user\" style=\"font-weight: bold;\"></span><span class=\"datetime secondary-text\" style=\"margin-left: 6px;\"><a href=\"https://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2018/08/comments-overflow-for-inoperative-load.html?showComment=1535398556183#c1061350286957344881\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">August 28, 2018 at 1:05 AM</a></span></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_70MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px;\">\nPranam Captain Ajit,<br />Sir if water has memory, and Axolotls have such phenomenal regenerative superpowers, then the water had this imprinted within, making it \"holier\" in its power than the Ganga waters.<br />Also, is it correct to assume Danavas were closer to Mayans and Aztecs than Vedics of the later period. mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;\">he advantage here is that<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"> pressures can be monitored from outside</i> the compartment.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;\">It can get very confusing when a LP alarm goes off in an enclosed compartment having more than one person with SCBA sets , whose air consumptions can vary, while say doing&nbsp;</span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;\">Methanol spray of a cargo tank.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">By the way NO regulation allows methanol spray with SCBA IBC sets. &nbsp;IBC sets are not &nbsp;for working in the literal sense. &nbsp;\" Working time \" relates to \"lung demand\" of free air, which is 10 litres / min for rest, 30 litres/ min for light work and 100 litres / min for strain of fireman's lift. Fill up a form in capital does NOT mean you have to take a flight to the capital city of your country. &nbsp;SCBA sets are for emergencies and must be donned by two sailors.</span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSquoHsLHWI/AAAAAAAACn8/0_UWNc6tv9c/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSquoHsLHWI/AAAAAAAACn8/0_UWNc6tv9c/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Air line breathing apparatus has been developed to enable compressed air equipment to be used for longer periods than would be possible using self contained equipment alone and to give easier access to confined compartments.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">The apparatus consists of a face mask supplied with moisture free compressed air through a small diameter air hose. Air, from a compressor is suitably filtered and its pressure reduced to the design pressure required to supply air to the face mask. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">Because of the small diameter of the air hose, it is essential that the air pressure not fall and the supply should be adjusted to maintain a constant pressure. The airhose must not be longer than 90 metres.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">The airhose should be non collapsible and kept clear of sharp projections. If the compressor fails to maintain this pressure, the supply must be switched over to compressed air bottles provided for such emergency. The user should then be signalled to leave the compartment.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">The air line pressure gauge and the control for changing over to an alternative supply must be under the constant supervision of a responsible person who has received instruction in the procedure required. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">It is recommended that a completely separate supply of clean air should be available under the direct control of the user. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">When using the equipment the following precautions are necessary: <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">The face mask must be checked and adjusted to ensure that it is airtight. The working air pressure should be checked before use. The audible low pressure alarm should be tested before use. The user should keep his air line clear of projections. The length of air hose used should not exceed 90 metres. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">If the user has reason to suspect the efficiency of the equipment he must leave the compartment immediately, switching over to an alternative supply of air, if available. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\"></span>Keep an EEBD/ ELSA handy . the hose must be attached to the wearer by a belt and must be quick disconnect system. The EEBD gives 40 litres/ min constant flow for 15 minutes and are ONLY for escape, never for working.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; mso-bidi-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>Airline systems must be examined and tested by a responsible ships officer at regular intervals. &nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;; font-size: large;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">On one of my chemical tankers the time charterers loved to stock cheap caustic SODA flakes in bags on my ship, as a tank cleaning chemical. &nbsp;</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Rt1LzaeZCQE/Ti_M-vlXtSI/AAAAAAAAEkk/CZMt8I9nWsI/s1600/imagesCA0ELOOA.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Rt1LzaeZCQE/Ti_M-vlXtSI/AAAAAAAAEkk/CZMt8I9nWsI/s1600/imagesCA0ELOOA.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">Now-- Caustic Soda is a good saponification agents for vegetable and animal fats. Saponification principle does NOT work for mineral oils at all .</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tCK6ROo_tZk/Ti_NFP49yzI/AAAAAAAAEko/eD59LZ56UAA/s1600/imagesCAX5OD21.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tCK6ROo_tZk/Ti_NFP49yzI/AAAAAAAAEko/eD59LZ56UAA/s1600/imagesCAX5OD21.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">Its only bad point is that it leaves a white stubborn residue of Calcium and Magnesium salts all over the tank.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHd1BOumI/AAAAAAAAClY/1ZcK1KmhuHQ/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHd1BOumI/AAAAAAAAClY/1ZcK1KmhuHQ/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHh7v86xI/AAAAAAAAClc/XV1DmJYg7zo/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHh7v86xI/AAAAAAAAClc/XV1DmJYg7zo/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">Caustic Potash/ NaOH does the same job as Caustic Potash/ KOH --with the added advantage that it does not leave the stubborn white marks.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-TY_wVUN6QY8/Ti_NJW8IklI/AAAAAAAAEks/VJpk3vw7_Po/s1600/imagesCA7O8Q7L.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-TY_wVUN6QY8/Ti_NJW8IklI/AAAAAAAAEks/VJpk3vw7_Po/s1600/imagesCA7O8Q7L.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">Both soda and potash converts the cargo residues to soap and glycerine .&nbsp;</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-u0rCPMGDw_Q/Ti_NPlykICI/AAAAAAAAEkw/feMVeRmJfWs/s1600/imagesCA66V9A7.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-u0rCPMGDw_Q/Ti_NPlykICI/AAAAAAAAEkw/feMVeRmJfWs/s1600/imagesCA66V9A7.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">KOH is stronger than NaOH and more soluble in alcohol. &nbsp;Soap remaining from Caustic Potash is easily washed away with water. Potassium soap is softer than sodium soap, and is used in shaving creams.</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHnb-sSqI/AAAAAAAAClg/yDt5H_Lxiu4/s1600/images+%25284%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHnb-sSqI/AAAAAAAAClg/yDt5H_Lxiu4/s1600/images+%25284%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHqyYsoVI/AAAAAAAAClk/RxdH2d7hQHE/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TSaHqyYsoVI/AAAAAAAAClk/RxdH2d7hQHE/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">Animal, fish and vegetable oils and fats as they are esters and are composed of glycerols and fatty acids which can be broken down by an alkali such as caustic potash. The fatty acids react with the caustic forming a soapy mixture which is soluble in water and thus simply washed away.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-D9agz93MQcY/Ti_NUww4FqI/AAAAAAAAEk0/0IsIGyQabgc/s1600/imagesCAUZKFH8.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-D9agz93MQcY/Ti_NUww4FqI/AAAAAAAAEk0/0IsIGyQabgc/s1600/imagesCAUZKFH8.jpg\" /></a></div><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">On Stainless steel ships, the white marks can be removed by Phosphoric acid recirc. On zinc and epoxy ships you can use Citric acid buffer solution whose pH is &gt; 5.5. &nbsp; But all this is added work when time is money.</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ovz1bhff8h8/Ti_NaGbg5FI/AAAAAAAAEk4/DIXdZo6OBZw/s1600/imagesCA3GNCY9.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ovz1bhff8h8/Ti_NaGbg5FI/AAAAAAAAEk4/DIXdZo6OBZw/s1600/imagesCA3GNCY9.jpg\" /></a></div><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">The following was copied to the Charterers who had the maturity to have a nice laugh, and took the message with grace .</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, understood and appreciated by my officers and crew--<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">ALL ENCLOSED LIFEBOATS CAN BE RELEASED OFF LOAD , AFTER THE BOAT HAS FLOATED ON WATER -- BY PUTTING ONE SINGLE FINGER OUTSIDE THROUGH THE FORD AND AFT PORTHOLES AND LIFTING UP A RESTRAINING BRIDLE . &nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">THERE IS NO NEED TO \"COLLAPSE\" THE HOOK AT ALL -- HENCE THERE IS NO NEED TO \"RESET\" THE HOOK EITHER.&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">THE MOMENT YOU LIFT IT UP THE BRIDLE FORD AND AFT WITH A SINGLE FINGER, THE BOAT GETS UNHOOKED-- LIKE MAGIC&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">AND FOR HOOKING ON TO THE NON-COLLAPSED HOOK -- YOU DON'T HAVE TO PUT THIS FINGER OUT TO LIFT THIS RESTRAINING BRIDLE -- THE RING GETS HOOKED ON BY ITSELF -- <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">pulling a single lever at coxswains seat -- to collapse two hooks ( ford+ aft ) simultaneously&nbsp; , 3 metres above water , on load , is fraught with danger.&nbsp; for both hooks will NEVER release at the same time --there will always be a microsecond time lag-- even if the release system is super intelligent. </span><o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">that is why on a trapeze act in a circus-- ONE man (hanging upside down) , lets the girl go -- and she does the magic turns in mid air.&nbsp; &nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">if TWO men were to hold one hand each -- she won\u2019t be doing any magic turns -- she will most probably fall down in a ugly heap --<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"color: red; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">A SINGLE LEVER SHOULD NEVER EVER RELEASE TWO HOOKS-- A POORLY ENGINEERED RELEASE MECHANISM SHOULD RELEASE ONLY ONE HOOK&nbsp; -- <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">enclosed LB always falls with 90 deg inclination.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">when one hook gives way-- the other hook temorarily holds till the boat&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">comes to 90 deg due to gravity -- and then shears off.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">at this angle existing seatbelts ( with people facing sideways ) are&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">ineffective. hence the spine injuries , broken necks and deaths.</span><br />\n<div><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br XXXX waters \u2013<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New to do anything after 35 years of such huge misery at sea ( grieving sons and wives ) ? <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">IF A TRAPEZE STRONG MAN HANGING UPSIDE DOWN , IN A CIRCUS , RELEASES THE GIRL WITH BOTH HANDS AT THE SAME TIME -- THE GIRL WILL GO TO THE INTENDED DESTINATION OF THE NEXT MANS HANDS AFTER A NEAT DOUBLE SOMERSAULT.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">IF HE RELEASES HIS RIGHT HAND LATER THAN THE LEFT HAND BY A NANO SECOND &nbsp;, LIKE WHAT HAPPENS WITH POORLY DESIGNED RELEASE MECHANICAL HOOKS -- THE GIRL WILL SWERVE OFF AND FALL OUTSIDE THE SAFETY NET.<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">this is what is happening at sea-- 3 years ago i , in my private &nbsp;capacity as a sailor, had written to XXX, XXX, XXX etc years ago !<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">-- who cares? <o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\">MOST IMPORTANT BOTTOM LINE OF THIS CENTURY AT SEA:
